</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr><td class="infobox-full-data" colspan="2"><div class="ib-country-fn"><div class="plainlist">
<ul><li><span class="anchor" id="inforefa"></span>a. <b><a href="#infoa">^</a></b> Native language.</li>
<li><span class="anchor" id="inforefb"></span>b. <b><a href="#infob">^</a></b> <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">Official language</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWiesehöfer2001119_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWiesehöfer2001119-17">[14]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="anchor" id="inforefc"></span>c. <b><a href="#infoc">^</a></b> Literary language in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Babylonia" title="Achaemenid Babylonia">Babylonia</a>.</li></ul>
</div></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Achaemenid</b> or the <b>Achaemenian Empire</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELavanPayneWeisweiler201617_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELavanPayneWeisweiler201617-18">[15]</a></sup> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Persian_language" title="Old Persian language">Old Persian</a>: <span lang="peo"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%F0%90%8E%A7%F0%90%8F%81%F0%90%8F%82%F0%90%8E%B6" title="wikt:𐎧𐏁𐏂𐎶">𐎧𐏁𐏂</a></span>, <span title="Old Persian (ca. 600-400 B.C.)-language romanization"><i lang="peo-Latn">Xšāça</i></span>, <abbr title="literal translation">lit.</abbr> 'The Empire'<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[16]</a></sup> or 'The Kingdom'<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[17]</a></sup>), also called the <b>First Persian Empire</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrosius20211_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrosius20211-21">[18]</a></sup> was an <a href="/wiki/History_of_Iran#Classical_antiquity" title="History of Iran">ancient Iranian empire</a> founded by <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_the_Great" title="Cyrus the Great">Cyrus the Great</a> in 550 BC. Based in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>, it was contemporarily the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_empires" title="List of largest empires">largest empire in history</a>, spanning a total of 5.5 million square kilometres (2.1 million square miles) from the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">ancient Egypt</a> in the west to the <a href="/wiki/Indus_River" title="Indus River">Indus Valley</a> in the east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Turchin_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Turchin-14">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taagepera_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Taagepera-15">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>Around the 7th century BC, the region of <a href="/wiki/Persis" title="Persis">Persis</a> in the southwestern portion of the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_plateau" title="Iranian plateau">Iranian plateau</a> was settled by the <a href="/wiki/Persians" title="Persians">Persians</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-book_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-book-22">[19]</a></sup> from Persis, Cyrus rose and defeated the <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">Median Empire</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Lydia" title="Lydia">Lydia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Neo-Babylonian_Empire" title="Neo-Babylonian Empire">Neo-Babylonian Empire</a>, marking the formal establishment of a new imperial polity under the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_dynasty" title="Achaemenid dynasty">Achaemenid dynasty</a>.
</p><p>The Achaemenid Empire is well-known for having imposed a successful model of centralized, bureaucratic administration; its multicultural policy; building infrastructure, such as <a href="/wiki/Royal_Road" title="Royal Road">road systems</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Chapar_Khaneh" title="Chapar Khaneh">postal system</a>; the use of an official language across its territories; and the development of civil services, including its possession of a large, professional army. Its advancements inspired the implement of similar styles of governance by various later empires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schmitt_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-schmitt-23">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>By 330 BC, the Achaemenid Empire was conquered in its entirety by <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(ancient_kingdom)" title="Macedonia (ancient kingdom)">Greek Macedonia</a> under <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a>, an ardent admirer of Cyrus the Great.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ulrich_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ulrich-24">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[22]</a></sup> With <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Alexander_the_Great" title="Death of Alexander the Great">Alexander's death</a> marking the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_period" title="Hellenistic period">Hellenistic period</a>, most of the empire's former territory fell to the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Ptolemaic_Kingdom" title="Ptolemaic Kingdom">Ptolemaic Kingdom</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">Seleucid Empire</a> following the <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_Triparadisus" title="Partition of Triparadisus">Partition of Triparadisus</a> in 321 BC. Hellenistic rule remained in place until the Iranian elites of the central plateau finally reclaimed power under the <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">Parthian Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-book_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-book-22">[19]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Achaemenid_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Achaemenian empire borrows its name from the ancestor of Cyrus the Great, the founder of the empire, <a href="/wiki/Achaemenes" title="Achaemenes">Achaemenes</a>. The term <i><span title="English-language text"><span lang="en">Achaemenid</span></span></i> means "of the family of the Achaemenis/Achaemenes" (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Persian_language" title="Old Persian language">Old Persian</a>: <span lang="peo"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%F0%90%8F%83%F0%90%8E%A7%F0%90%8E%A0%F0%90%8E%B6%F0%90%8E%B4%F0%90%8E%A1%F0%90%8F%81" title="wikt:𐏃𐎧𐎠𐎶𐎴𐎡𐏁">𐏃𐎧𐎠𐎶𐎴𐎡𐏁</a></span> <i>Haxāmaniš</i>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[23]</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Bahuvrihi" title="Bahuvrihi">bahuvrihi</a> compound translating to "having a friend's mind").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETavernier200717_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETavernier200717-27">[24]</a></sup> Achaemenes was himself a minor seventh-century ruler of the <a href="/wiki/Anshan_(Persia)" title="Anshan (Persia)">Anshan</a> in southwestern Iran, and a vassal of <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Assyria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enc_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-enc-28">[25]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template"><span style="white-space: nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot"><span title=" Dead link tagged March 2019">dead link</span></a></i>]</span></sup>
</p><p>Around 850 BC the original nomadic people who began the empire called themselves the <i>Parsa</i> and their constantly shifting territory <i>Parsua</i>, for the most part localized around Persis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-book_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-book-22">[19]</a></sup> The name "Persia" is a Greek and <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> pronunciation of the native word referring to the country of the people originating from <a href="/wiki/Persis" title="Persis">Persis</a> (Old Persian: <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%F0%90%8E%B1%F0%90%8E%A0%F0%90%8E%BC%F0%90%8E%BF" title="wikt:𐎱𐎠𐎼𐎿">𐎱𐎠𐎼𐎿</a>, <i>Pārsa</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enc_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-enc-28">[25]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Persian_language" title="Old Persian language">Persian</a> term <i>Xšāça</i> (<span title="Old Persian (ca. 600-400 B.C.)-language text"><span lang="peo"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1094882035">.mw-parser-output .script-Cprt{font-size:1.25em;font-family:"Segoe UI Historic","Noto Sans Cypriot",Code2001}.mw-parser-output .script-Hano{font-size:125%;font-family:"Noto Sans Hanunoo",FreeSerif,Quivira}.mw-parser-output .script-Latf,.mw-parser-output .script-de-Latf{font-size:1.25em;font-family:"Breitkopf Fraktur",UnifrakturCook,UniFrakturMaguntia,MarsFraktur,"MarsFraktur OT",KochFraktur,"KochFraktur OT",OffenbacherSchwabOT,"LOB.AlteSchwabacher","LOV.AlteSchwabacher","LOB.AtlantisFraktur","LOV.AtlantisFraktur","LOB.BreitkopfFraktur","LOV.BreitkopfFraktur","LOB.FetteFraktur","LOV.FetteFraktur","LOB.Fraktur3","LOV.Fraktur3","LOB.RochFraktur","LOV.RochFraktur","LOB.PostFraktur","LOV.PostFraktur","LOB.RuelhscheFraktur","LOV.RuelhscheFraktur","LOB.RungholtFraktur","LOV.RungholtFraktur","LOB.TheuerbankFraktur","LOV.TheuerbankFraktur","LOB.VinetaFraktur","LOV.VinetaFraktur","LOB.WalbaumFraktur","LOV.WalbaumFraktur","LOB.WeberMainzerFraktur","LOV.WeberMainzerFraktur","LOB.WieynckFraktur","LOV.WieynckFraktur","LOB.ZentenarFraktur","LOV.ZentenarFraktur"}.mw-parser-output .script-en-Latf{font-size:1.25em;font-family:Cankama,"Old English Text MT","Textura Libera","Textura Libera Tenuis",London}.mw-parser-output .script-it-Latf{font-size:1.25em;font-family:"Rotunda Pommerania",Rotunda,"Typographer Rotunda"}.mw-parser-output .script-Lina{font-size:1.25em;font-family:"Noto Sans Linear A"}.mw-parser-output .script-Linb{font-size:1.25em;font-family:"Noto Sans Linear B"}.mw-parser-output .script-Ugar{font-size:1.25em;font-family:"Segoe UI Historic","Noto Sans Ugaritic",Aegean}.mw-parser-output .script-Xpeo{font-size:1.25em;font-family:"Segoe UI Historic","Noto Sans Old Persian",Artaxerxes,Xerxes,Aegean}</style><span class="script-Xpeo">𐎧𐏁𐏂</span></span></span>), literally meaning "The Kingdom",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[26]</a></sup> was used to refer to the Empire formed by their multinational state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-name_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-name-30">[27]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Achaemenid_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Achaemenid_timeline">Achaemenid timeline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Achaemenid_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Achaemenid timeline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i><small><a href="/wiki/Astronomical_year_numbering" title="Astronomical year numbering">Astronomical year numbering</a></small></i>
</p>
